[8/12/2025 7:43 PM] zxshoe (pinned)
I guess I'll kick things off by gathering some info that we've leaked the last few months..

**Alicia 1200 by MrA**
Mini-ITX AGA PCB with a few (>400) SMD components pre-mounted.
Spec. mostly same as original A1200 with a few fixes for increased stability.

• 2MB CHIP RAM on board
• Clock port
• Buffered IDE
• Floppy header
• RTC
• SER/PAR-headers
• 2x Joy/Mouse standard
• AMI/PC PS/2 Keyboard/Mouse
• PCMCIA on back
• Stereo Phono jacks
• 15 pin DSUB video with internal switch (when used with internal scandoubler)
• Tornado v2 Expansion - local cpu bus, A1200 compatible with optional adapter board for existing accelerators
• Video Port Expansion, similar to A4000 video slot. Perfect for Plug & Play internal scandoubler Output automatically switched with 15kHz video
• Price TBA
• Available mid October

https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=O4LmU792x0Y

*From Sweden with Love*
🖖 🇸🇪 ❤️

[8/12/2025 8:21 PM] zxshoe
As a probable start of a FAQ: There are already a few projects ongoing to provide multiple accelerators and scan doubler options for Alicia 1200. 

MrA wen't out of his way to make the expansion busses as similar to existing designs as possible. This makes adopting an existing design to Alicia 1200's Tornado v2 and video port super easy. Basically just drag and drop our Tornado v2 schema symbol in place and routing should be very simple.

The Video Port has all the essential signals from an A4000 video slot. We will be releasing more details as well as schematics and design templates for Tornado v2 and the Video Port in the coming weeks.

Feel free to add to the FAQ 🖖 😉

[8/16/2025 6:04 PM] jaycee1980
its amazing how cheap the jellybean stuff can get


[8/16/2025 6:05 PM] jaycee1980
i shaved a good £20 off my psu simply by avoiding some values of resistor


[8/16/2025 6:08 PM] jaycee1980
for example the TPS54531 regulator datasheet specifies 10K2 as one of the resistors in the feedback divider. Switching that out for 10K and recalculating the other resistor saved quite a bit. Similarly avoiding 50K and using 49K9 was cheaper


[8/16/2025 6:10 PM] jaycee1980
another surprising one was swapping out an 1117-3.3 regulator for a HT7533-1


[8/16/2025 7:06 PM] zxshoe
Indeed. A lot of effort has been put into finding the optimal components for both Denise and Alicia 1200.


[8/16/2025 7:28 PM] jaycee1980
its amazing how much work it is but also quite amazing how much you can shave off 🙂

[8/25/2025 8:43 AM] zxshoe
As one of the points of Alicia 1200 is its formfactor it wouldn't make sense having an edge mounted accessory. 

The pin aligment of T2 is almost identical to the A1200 card edge slot. To make it super simple to adopt existing designs. 

We will release both an EDA schematic symbol as well as a template design to get people started. And there's already at least two different accelerators already produced for T2 😉  (more info on that "soon")

We hope the flexibility it provides will inspire several accessories like a true 24-bit scandoubler among other things.

[9/3/2025 6:07 PM] djbase

[9/3/2025 6:08 PM] djbase
so gives a little extra boost

[9/7/2025 7:04 PM] zxshoe
**Another small teaser of what's to come!**

The new A1200-T2 card edge adapter have now been QA tested and as expected checks out ✅ 
On this image a Blizzard 1260 was stress tested running Quake and some demanding AGA/060 demos.

{Attachments}
https://cdn.discordapp.com/attachments/1404852770154217664/1414295227555909743/b1260adp_01.jpg?ex=69abb1d2&is=69aa6052&hm=d1cb90eca9e51cfb07d51b3957450f863367308e644387cb635c2305ceca2c9c&

{Reactions}
❤️ (5) 👀 (2) 😍

[9/7/2025 7:08 PM] zxshoe
I'm hoping the community (looking at **you** 🫵) will assist in creating suitable 3D print models for different existing accessories.
The mounting holes on the motherboard are aligned to be used for this purpose as well as the upcoming native T2 accelerators from 3:rd parties 🖖 🇸🇪  ❤️

Since some cards have the CPU on "top" in the original A1200 case and others on the bottom a choice had to be made. This is what you're looking at. _However_ the Tornado v2 connector luckily exists in several flavors providing more space if a heat sink and/or fan is needed.

{Reactions}

[9/21/2025 2:21 PM] zxshoe
This is rev1.4 of the board and there's been a few changes on the upcoming production version rev1.6

If you look closely you'll see two blue wires next to the T2 expansion. This is obviously fixed on r1.6. As we'll as a couple of added and modified resistors to clean up clock and video signals. 

Also - the IDE buffers have been removed to minimize the risk of incompatible with expansions like the FastATA. Most IDE adapters today already have the buffer circuts anyway.

We're trying to keep Alicia 1200 as close to the original as possible minus some bugs of course 🖖 😁 🇸🇪 ❤️

[9/22/2025 3:44 PM] zxshoe (pinned)
So basically the big one is the same local bus expansion as the A1200 but on a 120-pin JAE connector similar to the big box Amigas. We're calling this Tornado v2 or just T2. The idea is to include these as options when ordering a board. 

Pin arrangement is 1:1 with the original so adapting current designs to it should be very straight forward. In addition a few extra nice to have signals are included. So a Zorro 2 adapter would be possible for example. 

The smaller 50-pin connector is the Video Port. Inspired by the A4000 video connector (more info on this later), trust me it is **awesome** and you're going to love it! 🖖 🇸🇪 ❤️


[9/22/2025 3:46 PM] zxshoe
@Chrissy feel free to pin the above post 👆

[9/23/2025 2:05 PM] karlosjackel
You won't be disappointed! We've been testing the REV1.4, and its pretty awesome! We have been testing various accelerators, and results are being fed back to @zxshoe and MrA. Obvs, the 1.6 will be better than the 1.4 through this feedback and MrA's continuous improvements to the system. 

If you are torn between the ReAmiga and the Alicia, the Alicia in my honest opinion was the easier build - Its all done for you [the birdseed and most of the logic chips at least]! Soldering those J legs do take some practice, but even on the layout of the memory chips there is considerable more space for soldering then on the original A1200. 

If I had my way, I'd build these over the ReAmiga A1200 - But, there is something about the wedge isn't there? 😄 I've built a couple of ReAmigas A1200s, repaired a few original A1200s, so I feel I've got a good reference to go on. Its all my own opinion anyways.. Its ANOTHER AMIGA! And there is NOTHING wrong in MORE AMIGAS!! 😄

[10/30/2025 3:30 PM] zxshoe
Hey buddy! Glad to hear you're excited 🤩 

So I've been back and forth on this for a few weeks. Due to the financial risk of ordering lots of PCB's with +450 components from China a pre-order/payment was considered.

However - as some of you know my personal health is not the best and the (self induced) stress of having charged anyone in advance - and then wanting to ship board as soon as humanly possible - is simply not a good recipe for me.

But thanks to everyone who bought Denise recently and the small batch of Alicia 1200 r1.6 presented at AMIGA40 in Germany I now feel the best approach is to keep the same setup as before.

So the plan is to order the boards. Verify the batch. And then sell kits like before in smaller batches of 10-20 at a time. As well as provide boards for UK and US markets thanks to our excellent friends @Derek🇬🇧  &  @Stefan R 🇺🇸

It's a lot harder than you think to set dates for things like this 😉 but my hope to at least get some of you an Alicia 1200 under the Christmas tree.
🎅 🎁🎄


[10/30/2025 3:38 PM] zxshoe (pinned)
I've been asked a couple of times what parts are needed in addition to the ones already on the board.

When purchasing a kit from us, you'll also get access to a manual and BOM. Here all pre mounted components (~450 of them) will be marked. **No through hole parts are included, so things like sockets and headers you will have to buy and mount yourself. As well as the CPU, AGA chipset, RAM and a few other components. **When I ordered everything (except AGA ICs) from Digikey it came to about €80. So it's not super expensive.

edit: Since interest in _Alicia 1200_ seems to be high we've [**decided to share the BOM so everyone**](https://nextcloud.syntaxsociety.se/index.php/s/R3twMwanY6oLrHd) get time to prepare and look at what's needed, etc. **Please note: A FEW COMPONENTS MIGHT DIFFER BETWEEN BATCHES**, for instance batch 1 of r1.6 might be missing U8 on the back while batch 2 r1.6 might not. Obviously we do our very best to avoid this, but in order to avoid long production delays - we've decided to allow small differences. You can still get things like connectors, TH components, sockets, if you want.

As always - if you're unsure about anything - just ask.

{Embed}
https://nextcloud.syntaxsociety.se/index.php/s/R3twMwanY6oLrHd

[11/1/2025 6:03 PM] jbilander
What I tend to do now with PLCC sockets is to take the base out so that soldering is easy and solid and then I tape the base back in with a double coated tape that is like 1 mm thick, to the left in pic here

{Attachments}
https://cdn.discordapp.com/attachments/1404852770154217664/1434226443318988880/image.png?ex=69abb1b6&is=69aa6036&hm=35f4ef2cf0e61116b45436a18fa5af72bd581771de5d41dd110a8f121b75383c&


[11/1/2025 6:04 PM] jbilander
the tape also elevates the base somewhat and hence the chip sits at a perfect position when installed. I have discovered that with the PLCC32 sockets the chip sometimes sinks too deep into a standard PLCC32-socket (even with the base left in) rendering in bad contact with some pins.

{Reactions}
👍

Also an observation on the board itself - the part references on the silkscreen are within the footprints of the chips. This is probably great for clarity when building but then as soon as the chips are installed they're covered up, which is not ideal for troubleshooting afterwards as you can't see at a glance which is which.

[11/8/2025 1:59 AM] jaycee1980

[11/8/2025 2:03 AM] jaycee1980
tbh you dont really need a specific schematic to troubleshoot clock issues, the standard A1200 schematic will tell you that. Make sure 28MHz goes into pin 94 of Budgie, and comes out again on pin 95. After that, check it gets to pin 25 of Lisa, and that you get two clocks on 22/23 of Lisa into pins 34/36 of Alice. Alice should generate its set of clocks from there


[11/8/2025 2:04 AM] jaycee1980
budgie creates the 14MHz CPU clock from !CDAC and 7MHz iirc

{Reactions}
👍

[11/15/2025 3:08 AM] seb132
DEMON 1260 Specs:
68060 CPU card with synchronous bus design, clock frequency adjustable via software up to >100MHz
Modern FPGA-based design without legacy CPLD components
256 MB SDRAM
MAPROM function for soft kick, or 68EC060 CPUs without MMU
M.2 SATA interface for on-board mass storage
Flash ROM for IDE drivers and system startup
Temperature-controlled PWM fan control
Local full-speed 32-bit expansion bus, auto-configuring, up to 512MB address space
Connection for WIFI module, 4MBaud serial interface communication
Battery-buffered real-time clock!
Design files freely available, commercially available from Alinea Computer 

Translated with DeepL.com (free version)

{Reactions}

[11/15/2025 7:03 PM] jbilander
Many accelerator boards, Blizzard, GVP, ACA500plus, ACA1221lc, Furia EC020 etc include custom "glue-logic" (in a CPLD or FPGA) that handles the memory mapping, then no MMU is required.

{Reactions}
👍

[11/15/2025 7:03 PM] jbilander
I guess that is what is meant here.


[11/15/2025 7:04 PM] jbilander
This approach is hardware-specific and relies on software provided by the board manufacturer (like ACAtool or Blizkick).


[11/15/2025 7:05 PM] jbilander
If you don't have such a feature on the accelerator card then you can use the MMU-based "FastROM" functionality provided the CPU has a MMU.


[11/15/2025 7:56 PM] zxshoe
Interesting, thanks


[11/16/2025 9:54 AM] jbilander
No problem, the only little annoying thing with blizkick as I experienced it (when I used it in my blizzard III card) was the automatic soft reboot that it does on cold boot startup.


[11/16/2025 9:55 AM] jbilander
When the amiga is powered on and the blizkick command is run early in the startup-sequence the program loads your KS image into fast ram, then performs an automatic soft reboot and at the second boot (and any following Ctrl-A-A resets) it detects that the new valid ROM image is already present in the fast ram and enables the mapROM function.


[11/16/2025 9:58 AM] jbilander
I think a more elegant solution would be to have a shadow ram (maybe a dedicated 1 MB SRAM chip on board) that would not be mapped as fast ram to the Amiga OS but to be used as a dedicated fastROM (behind the scene).


[11/16/2025 9:59 AM] jbilander
The KS image could be stored in the FPGA's spi flash memory and copied by the FPGA to the SRAM before the CPU and the rest of the system comes up.


[11/16/2025 10:04 AM] jbilander
As soon as the copying is done the mapROM function would be enabled in the FPGA (if a jumper is set).

{Reactions}
🖖

[11/20/2025 9:20 AM] zxshoe
👆  Exactly this. Imo PiStorm setup is _very easy_ compared to installing and setting up an expanded Classic Amiga. I've used and set up everything from A1200/PPC/BVision (AmigaOS _and_ Linux/X11) to A4000T with Mediator/NIC/Voodoo5500-RTG/MPEG/SB/etc. Now THAT was challenging.

Not to simplify your problems @Retro4U (Neil), but for PiStorm there's very good tools to automate all of that. I used https://mja65.github.io/Emu68-Imager and it does _everything_ for you in one go. Just a couple of clicks. What used to take a whole weekend is now done in minutes.

Using ready made .hdf is an option, but then you get what the designer intended and you don't have a clue about what's actually happening in the background. Taking the time to read up on the details helps alot when things go south. And believe me, they will 😉 _"Only AMIGA makes it possible" 😆

{Embed}
https://mja65.github.io/Emu68-Imager
Welcome to the Emu68 Imager.

[11/24/2025 6:13 AM] mc68060
If Polymer, then I also only would use hybrid polymers. Solid polymers don't have the self healing effect like regular electrolytes or hybrid polymers


[11/24/2025 12:07 PM] jaycee1980
the top reason for using them is often "they dont leak" but well.. we dont know what the long term failure mode of polymers is

{Reactions}
😂

[11/24/2025 11:17 PM] seb132
I hope they don’t fly out of their motherboards like Russian rockets ! 😄

{Reactions}
🫡 🇺🇸 🇷🇺

[11/25/2025 7:29 AM] mc68060
It's quite good understood. For solid polymers / conductive polymers even backed by >30 years of in field usage 🙂 the mentioned hybrid polymer (which a favourable for many reasons over solid polymers  in e.g. automotive) it looks a bit different, as they emerged around 2010ish . But on the other hand we don't have any measurable evidence at work that we ever had a field failure with the hybrid polymers we use (Panasonic something something). But the same applies for good quality regular electrolytes (Rubycon ZLK/ZLJ) . The later we build into ECUs which we  produced since 10 years , roundabout 1.5mio ECUs per year , with 5 ZLK/ZLJ per ECU 🙂

{Reactions}
🤘 👍

[11/25/2025 11:24 AM] jaycee1980
ok fair enough. Still no point in using them in an Amiga though, IMO 🙂


[11/25/2025 11:24 AM] jaycee1980
provided you use good quality electrolytics there will be no problems 🙂


[11/25/2025 11:25 AM] jaycee1980
the main thing polymers are good for is their extended temperature range and their very low ESR. Neither really matter in an Amiga


[11/25/2025 11:26 AM] jaycee1980
i quite often use Rubycon YXJ/YXF for regular stuff


[11/25/2025 11:33 AM] mc68060
Yes also my stance. If you need low ESR, low leakage and have high ripple currents  : hybrid polymers. For everything else regular aluminium electrolyte from good manufacturers.


[11/25/2025 1:38 PM] jaycee1980
@Claude ive found properly derated MLCC ceramics are good for ultralow ESR.. though i guess in an automotive environment they would not be due to risk of fracture


[11/25/2025 1:39 PM] jaycee1980
not that i know how to properly derate them yet 😉 I've used them on my usb pd power supply though and the ripple on the output is super tiny


[11/25/2025 1:39 PM] mc68060
Yeah we can use mlcc too 🙂 but usually only flexiterm or flexisafe types


[11/25/2025 1:40 PM] mc68060

[11/25/2025 1:41 PM] mc68060

[12/21/2025 1:36 PM] jaycee1980

[12/21/2025 5:40 PM] rik3i
Small progress.. I haven't yet reflowed Budgie since it looks fine, although there was a nice tiny splodge of wicked(?) solder near the term resistors for DS(?) easily removed with a tooth pick.
Read through the Re-Amiga 1200 build guide for inspiration, cross-referenced the DRAM with PCB locator for A1200 (caveat: chips not in same order, alternate pairs for *CAS lines). Fixed a couple of pins that didn't have continuity, quite confident the full set are soldered now.
Bypassed the MAX to Paula for serial but didn't get a hint of anything at all (vs. garbage on the port), so that's a bit weird.

[12/23/2025 11:55 AM] mc68060
i think some of the higher databus pins are either stuck or floating. D31..D24 (cpu side) or DRD31..DRD24 (chipmem bus side). thats where paula gets it's serial data from, and when there is only garbage on serial (and probably also the wrong baudrate) then this is a indication where the problem is

{Reactions}
👍 ❤️

[12/23/2025 11:56 AM] mc68060

[12/23/2025 11:57 AM] mc68060
as diagrom seems to "boot" fine up to serial output the problem is probably not the cpu side directly

[12/30/2025 8:52 PM] rik3i
Still working through *leftover turkey* here 🫣  I made a quick map of the chips in KiCad which I hope is mostly accurate (!) and probed/scoped practically everything interesting here, plus the GAL and DRAMs etc.
Nothing standing out as a problem (to me) but learning a lot about the machine from A1200 schematics where I can map between Alicia. One thing I have noticed is that /RAMEN is never asserted, but not sure I expect it to until Diagrom starts executing RAM tests; the DRAM itself seems to be happily refreshing in the background. Similarly, /DSACK0 had an odd range (2-4V) at Gayle but I think makes sense because the GAL is driving for long/ROM reads and there's a 68 ohm resistor on the path so, not so weird?! Working through a whole lot of this kind of thing 😅

[1/15/2026 6:35 PM] zxshoe
The educational and community parts of this projects are the most important, at least for me. I can assure you that you'll be able to learn and enjoy the ins and outs of the AGA chipsets 100% with this build. MrA's Mini-ITX design is unique in several ways - but it's still an AGA machine. The excellent schematics available at https://www.amigapcb.org and other places are in many ways very usable.

And I just realized that I forgot to post yesterday about adding the new and excellent [Alicia 1200 Schematics & Troubleshooting.pdf to the Dev/ folder on the file share.](https://nextcloud.syntaxsociety.se/index.php/s/R3twMwanY6oLrHd) In this document most if not all aspects that's special about Alicia is documented with schematics.

{Embed}
https://www.amigapcb.org/
Amiga PCB Explorer
The Amiga PCB Explorer is a browser application that was designed to assist people in various aspects of Amiga mainboard repairs.
https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/Pu2b1NtuJ8PXfQYgLcfTmdZzJ4RvPw9rfR6q_fECugc/http/www.amigapcb.org/gfx/a500r8a.png

{Embed}
https://nextcloud.syntaxsociety.se/index.php/s/R3twMwanY6oLrHd

Syntax Society - If you build it, they will come

[1/15/2026 6:47 PM] zxshoe
**Also a short update about ETA on the next batch Alicia 1200 boards**

Alicia 1200MkII (r2.0) is now a 6 layer board with _even better_ signal integrity than before! Builders of r1.6 was amazed over the video quality from Alicia, and now this has improved even further. The BOM has not changed between r1.6 and r2.0 but components _have moved around_ a bit. Also due to availability the pre soldered SMD's _may vary slightly_. I'll try to make this as clear as possible in the BOM for r2.0.

We placed the order this week. So expect boards to be added to Tindie in about a month. **Thank you all for your patience and support!!**
Just like before I'll probably add boards 10 at a time, and another batch after this one is already planned. So don't worry, just like with Denise - everybody who wants a board will get a board 🖖😃🍻

[1/17/2026 12:41 PM] zxshoe
Functionally nothing. The BOM is the same as before. But as I wrote according to tests the video output is _even sharper_ than before (and not as sensitive to low quality PSUs as r1.4/1.6.) And that's saying something as the 4 layer board was noticeably better than an original A1200. Lastly I've been told that the custom chips run a bit cooler, probably thanks to the extra copper in the layers below. I might get corrected on some of this as I don't have my own board just yet. But this is what I know so far.

[1/17/2026 4:13 PM] zxshoe
**A quick note on the r1.0 T2-A1200-adapter:** If you happen to have an accelerator that does not work out of the box with the adapter; there's a simple patch that will fix the issue! Information is provided in the [Alicia 1200 r1.6 folder on Nextcloud.](https://nextcloud.syntaxsociety.se/index.php/s/R3twMwanY6oLrHd)

The new adapter (r1.1) produced with the upcoming batch of Alicia's of course have this patch included. And so far we haven't found an A1200 accelerator card that doesn't work perfectly* on Alicia 1200.
_** If a card takes up a lot of space towards the motherboard an extended version of the T2-adapter connector can be used to make room for airflow. This is the case for BlizzardPPC or when using an Indivision AGA._

{Embed}
https://nextcloud.syntaxsociety.se/index.php/s/R3twMwanY6oLrHd

[1/19/2026 3:02 PM] zxshoe

[1/19/2026 6:49 PM] ndjordjevic5067
Can someone briefly summarize, in couple sentences, the differences between the real amiga 1200 and Alicia. Tnx


[1/19/2026 7:01 PM] brainfood.
my uneducated take on the differences between an amiga 1200 and the Alicia is that the Alicia has a mini ITX form factor, meaning the board is small and it can all fit in a small mini ITX supported pc case, The power uses ATX style power connector meaning it can be powered using a typical PC powersupply. The Alica supports PS/2 style keyboard and mouse.


[1/19/2026 9:20 PM] rickwarlock
And superior image quality. A video slot, basic ZII support on the local bus. Built-in Video Switch, clean PCMCIA fix. Small ‘bug’ fixes compared to A1200. Excellent signal integrity. Better cooling capacity. ESD protection.


[1/20/2026 12:42 AM] zxshoe
Like @brainfood. And @RickWarlock already mentioned the key differences are the **Mini-ITX form factor** and the fact that Alicia 1200 is sold as a **DIY project.** Not a finished product from us.

Other technical differences are • Amiga and PS/2 mouse with scroll wheel support • Amiga _and_ PS/2 keyboard support • 6-Layer High Quality PCB • Superior audio and video quality • BigROM and dual kickstarts switchable from keyboard • Several bugs fixed from the original • ESD protected ports • Buffered sync signals to protect Alice IC • More robust and backwards compatible expansion port (Tornado v2) including ZII signals • A4000® inspired Video Port with automatic monitor switch on DB15 VGA connector • Serial and Parallel ports on headers • On board RTC • Intelligent floppy detection to speed up boot procedure.

All included SMD components (~60 different, >450 in total) are carefully selected after meticulous calculations and testing by de designer MrA.

Other standard features like • Floppy • IDE • PCMCIA • Clock port • MC68020 CPU • 2MB CHIP RAM and AGA Chipset are of course the same as the original.

Perhaps I forgot something 😆 but basically Alicia 1200 includes most of the "fixes" and add-ons needed for a "modern" AGA system.


[1/20/2026 12:46 AM] zxshoe
This is a truly project of passion. Matured and developed over the course of over a decade. 

From Sweden with ❤️


[1/20/2026 12:54 AM] rickwarlock
I couldn't go back to the image produced by an Amiga 1200 or even an Amiga 4000. Alicia, and MkII in particular, are in a completely different league. You have to see it to believe it.

[2/12/2026 6:19 PM] zxshoe
Hi, cool project! Short answer: no. The external PS/2 connector always goes through the MCU. The CIA signals are not exposed directly and there is no dedicated header for this purpose.

However, if your keyboard emulation is 100% compatible as an A4000 keyboard it will work fine on both Denise and Alicia.

The keyboard implementations are not identical on both systems (different implementation/firmware). but everything is documented and the necessary bits you need are in the schematics available on the share in the pinned post in this channel and #denise-pcb should you need it.

But the short answer is: If it works on an A4000 it should work on MrA's boards 🖖😁

{Reactions}

[2/13/2026 1:00 PM] mc68060
Self resonance point is at ~100MHz usually that way 🙂 ~150nh per cm of ground wire , ~ 15pf in 10:1 mode on good probes . With a high du/dt signal like from a CMOS oscillator this gets funky:) that's why you can easily shelf out 200-300€ for a single 350MHz passive probe alone . At work we hack sometimes something, using a bnc to probe tip adapter (10-15€) and twisted enameld wire to measure directly on chips when a high slew rate signal needs to be measured . Here a 11V +/- 300mA gate drive signal . Ground picked up locally at the ASIC , gate drive signal also more or less directly.

{Attachments}
https://cdn.discordapp.com/attachments/1404852770154217664/1471838532514611362/rn_image_picker_lib_temp_c676ef5d-9d9d-4dea-8aa7-e0f0d6ef2ef7.jpg?ex=69ab6ab3&is=69aa1933&hm=4b33b4e09e51c774b9a6892d71ed1f319858ca774781cb62e676f534fbfb5b7d&

{Reactions}
😍 🖖

[2/13/2026 1:37 PM] jaycee1980
the main takeaway here is, if youre measuring something like a clock signal or something high speed, absolutely dont use the ground lead on your probe 😉 Unless youre only checking its present (well.. for anything youd find in an Amiga anyway)


[2/13/2026 1:38 PM] jaycee1980
because the ground lead has inductance and that will make the signal look like it has overshoot/undershoot and ringing it may not actually have


[2/13/2026 1:45 PM] mc68060
Yes and frequency vs slew rate 🙂 a 1MHz square wave can make more headaches then a whatever gigahertz sine 🙂

[2/17/2026 7:46 PM] jaycee1980
i really question the value of doing a board completely through hole


[2/17/2026 8:05 PM] zxshoe
Listen, before I dared venture into SMD I was all in on Through Hole. I even felt those who claimed that SMD soldering was "easier" than TH was being smug.

But now - after using a microscope for a couple of weeks I really do get it! Thorough hole is a pain! 😅 but those of you who've been doing this for 20+ years might not remember what it was like not knowing..

I assume you're referring to Easy-Amy being 99% TH. And even here MrA realised that making this board with TH components resulted in the opposite! It was a PAIN to build 😆 

So the next revision of Easy-Amy will probably have most SMD's mounted from factory. And focus on mounting sockets for the custom OCS chipset and connectors.

👍

[2/17/2026 8:14 PM] jaycee1980
the biggest obstacle with SMD i found, was learning to forget what you know about TH soldering for it

for example youre taught not to bring solder to the joint - but thats exactly what you do on SMD soldering


[2/17/2026 8:15 PM] jaycee1980
oh and not trying to solder each individual pin on a chip... flux and drag 🙂

[2/23/2026 12:52 PM] rik3i
I found a Lattice tech note "Solder Reflow Guide for Surface Mount Devices" with a table, and they suggest ~235/260 (Pb/-free) for peak reflow (was a bit less for earlier rev of the note). But at that temp, around 1-2mins maximum along with decent preheating. Wouldn't want to risk any higher than that tbh


[2/23/2026 12:57 PM] rik3i
Now I have a hot air station on its way I really want to try to see if it helps, but shall be going low; enough to maybe take out any crusty flux I couldn't get near with a brush 🫠


[2/23/2026 1:42 PM] brainfood.

[2/24/2026 1:42 PM] lensrev
What is the difference (if any) for the Tornado V2? Or is it derived from proto to production release?


[2/24/2026 6:17 PM] zxshoe
The first connector we called "Tornado" was totally different and was only on the earlierst r1.0/1.2 prototypes. It was later changed to the one we have now. Hence the V2. Tornado is only a made up name and nothing official, it's only to clarify that it's for the Alicia 1200.


[2/24/2026 6:20 PM] zxshoe
This was the first version of Tornado (never released)

{Attachments}
https://cdn.discordapp.com/attachments/1404852770154217664/1475905324664881232/image.png?ex=69abb5b2&is=69aa6432&hm=e445dc2f49ca84b120ee20b633293cec42a56aeb9d7027460d1f78a80f9ad8dc&

{Reactions}
👍

[2/24/2026 6:26 PM] zxshoe
Funny anecdote; on Tornado v1 PCMCIA and video signals were also on the connector. An adapter was made to add PCMCIA. This concept was later scrapped in favor of putting it back on the motherboard as well as introducing the _Video Port_ aka "VP2" which is a dedicated 50-pin TX24-50R from the same family as T2.

{Attachments}
https://cdn.discordapp.com/attachments/1404852770154217664/1475906809347706982/image.png?ex=69abb714&is=69aa6594&hm=c3179a81480726d7051a6afac30c8df2f7c09439cea33ff0aee35c2cabcc3805&


[2/24/2026 6:27 PM] zxshoe
Hope I don't confuse you all now 😄 To be crystal clear - **The above stuff is for HISTORICAL purpose** and nothing current 🙂


[2/24/2026 6:28 PM] zxshoe
Also to show the enormous amount of work that's been put into this project over the past +10 years.

[2/25/2026 7:39 AM] zxshoe

The reasons for the switch I was told was mainly cost and availability at the time. Plus the factor that the other one felt and looked more Amiga-y 🙃 since it reassembles the big box CPU connector. 

It was also smaller and having a dedicated Video connector was more convenient.

[2/25/2026 10:44 PM] zxshoe
If you haven't tried the T2 connector I can tell you that it's really really nice. It has those _bevels_ that helps with orientation and a very satisfying "click" when you push it all the way. It also helps keeping it in place, unlike the darn CPU-slots on big box Amigas. Lol, adjusting the accelerator every single time I moved my A4kT somewhere 😆

Like me and @Tim'sRetro learned the hard way; the male T2 connector that sits on the T2-A1200-Adapter and upcoming accelerators _can_ crack if mounted the wrong way. So don't force it. And watch for the _notch_ like @Chucky points out in his guide.

{Reactions}

[2/28/2026 12:30 PM] zxshoe
I don't want to argue, I do agree the prices are extreme! But as there is an option to their stock (purchase a 2:nd hand, preferably broken A1200 and desolder the ICs) I do understand their incentive to charge for their _rare_ parts. You don't **have to** buy from them. Having said that - had this been the case with clean water or something like that I'd obviously be of another opinion.

More importantly I think; their stock is very limited (I'm honestly guessing <10 kits) so they're not interested or able to sell a lot. Just look at the few people holing on to the last stock of rev 6 68060's. That's one IC for €350-400 these days. They also used to be much cheaper a few years ago. This is not unusual.

So, I'm sorry if that upsets you. But that's my honest opinion and I do think it's a valid discussion as the problem is not going away 🙂

Testing memory prior to soldering in all components, this is what i have does it seem correct?
pin 1 - continuity between all chips
pins 2 - 10 continuity between chip pairs
pins 11 -12  resistance between pins and pins on ALICE
pin 13 continuity between chip pairs
pins 14 -15 resistance between pins and pins on ALICE
pins 16 - 19 continuity between chip pairs
pin 20 - 21  continuity between all chips
pin 22 - 30 continuity between chip pairs
pin 31 no continuity between chips, no resistance to ALICE
pins 32 - 33 continuity between chip pairs
pins 34 - 40 continuity between all chips

Are you sure your monitor can handle 15kHz? You mentioned hdmi cable, that almost certainly won't work.

Even most VGA->HDMI converters will only work with 31kHz signal.

You need a monitor that can handle 15kHz _or_ use a scandoubler like DCE ScanMagic or Indivision AGA.

[3/4/2026 6:12 PM] zxshoe


{Forwarded Message}
**A quick note on the r1.0 T2-A1200-adapter:** If you happen to have an accelerator that does not work out of the box with the adapter; there's a simple patch that will fix the issue! Information is provided in the [Alicia 1200 r1.6 folder on Nextcloud.](https://nextcloud.syntaxsociety.se/index.php/s/R3twMwanY6oLrHd)

The new adapter (r1.1) produced with the upcoming batch of Alicia's of course have this patch included. And so far we haven't found an A1200 accelerator card that doesn't work perfectly* on Alicia 1200.
_** If a card takes up a lot of space towards the motherboard an extended version of the T2-adapter connector can be used to make room for airflow. This is the case for BlizzardPPC or when using an Indivision AGA._
Originally sent: 1/17/2026 4:13 PM

Lol, you and me both apparently 😄 But yes, the answer to your question is also in the manual 😉 

> **Serial and Parallel Ports**
> Based on headers, it provides a 25-pin parallel port and a 9-pin serial port.
> The connector is IDC-style, so be careful when buying a ready-made cable, as there are at least two standards.
> You should get a cable that is IDC standard or you can easily press your own cables with a bench vise.
